      Issues

Petronijević Terzić has argued that opposition parties should work on
covering all polling stations with controllers and bring abstainers and
those that are undecided, but also opposed the outgoing government, to
the polls.^[99] <#cite_note-:06-99> Shortly before the election was
called, Bursać has also predicted that the campaign would be filled with
"negative topics" such as the ongoing tensions with Kosovo, jeopardised
foreign policy positions due to the tensions with Kosovo, rising prices,
and the mass shootings that occurred in May 2023.^[99] <#cite_note-:
06-99> Vojislav Mihailović of CRTA has said that opposition parties
should put local politics, economy, corruption, crime and violence, as
its main topics while campaigning, while he also said that "citizens are
most concerned about economic issues" in opinion polls that CRTA
conducted.^[288] <#cite_note-289>

Bojan Bilbija, a /Politika <https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Politika>/
journalist, Zoran Panović, a Demostat journalist, and Miloš Garić, the
editor-in-chief of /Kosovo Online/, all agreed that economic issues and
the North Kosovo crisis would be the main issues of the elections.^[289]
<#cite_note-290> Vladimir Pejić, the director of Agency Faktor Plus,
listed the North Kosovo crisis, economic issues, and the fight against
crime and corruption as the main issues of the election.^[290]
<#cite_note-291> Milivojević and political consultant Nikola Tomić named
Kosovo as the "absolutely dominant" issue for the upcoming
elections.^[291] <#cite_note-292> Klačar named living standards,
inflation and prices, Kosovo, foreign policy positions, and European
Union membership as main issues.^[292] <#cite_note-293> Boban Stojanović
listed living standards, inflation, and Kosovo as main topics, also
claiming that "there will also be enormous pressure on SNS voters, on
public sector employees, and blackmailing".^[293] <#cite_note-294>


      Party campaigns

According to the preliminary report of the Agency for the Prevention of
Corruption from 14 December, SNS spent € <https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/
Euro>4,500,000 during the campaign period, SPS spent € <https://
en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euro>1,600,000 while VMSZ spent around € <https://
en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euro>100,000.^[294] <#cite_note-:46-295> From the
opposition, Serbia on the West alliance spent more than € <https://
en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euro>200,000, SPN spent € <https://
en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euro>82,000, Narodna spent € <https://
en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euro>46,000, We–The Voice from the People
<https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/We%E2%80%93The_Voice_from_the_People>
spent € <https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euro>4,490, and SRS spent €
<https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euro>1,500.^[294] <#cite_note-:46-295>
From minority parties, the Russian Party <https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/
Russian_Party_(Serbia)> spent € <https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/
Euro>162,000.^[294] <#cite_note-:46-295>


        Serbian Progressive Party

Aleksandar Vučić at the Russian Duma in Moscow, Russia in 2019 <https://
en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Aleksandar_Vu%C4%8Di%C4%87_2019_(cropped).jpg>
Despite no longer being president of SNS, Vučić has mainly represented
the party throughout the election campaign

Vučević announced that SNS would begin its campaign in late October,
after the 15-year anniversary of the founding assembly of SNS.^[295]
<#cite_note-296> Despite this, SNS organised gatherings with its
supporters before the 15-year celebration to promote the party for the
upcoming elections.^[296] <#cite_note-297> SNS received an endorsement
by its former president Vučić, saying that "he will not stay on the
sideline and will not be neutral"; he also announced that Tomislav
Nikolić <https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tomislav_Nikoli%C4%87>, former
president of Serbia and president of SNS, would also participate in the
campaign.^[297] <#cite_note-298> ^[298] <#cite_note-299> Stefan
Krkobabić <https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stefan_Krkobabi%C4%87>, the
leader of Party of United Pensioners of Serbia <https://
en.wikipedia.org/wiki/PUPS_%E2%80%93_Solidarity_and_Justice> (PUPS) in
the National Assembly, also expressed his support for SNS and said that
PUPS would campaign on introducing a guaranteed social pension <https://
en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Social_pension>.^[299] <#cite_note-300> The
Strength of Serbia Movement <https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/
Strength_of_Serbia_Movement>, a SNS ally since 2010,^[300]
<#cite_note-301> announced that they would not contest the 2023
parliamentary election; the Serbian Renewal Movement <https://
en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Serbian_Renewal_Movement> of Vuk Drašković
<https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vuk_Dra%C5%A1kovi%C4%87> did not sign a
cooperation agreement with SNS for the 2023 election but they also
announced that two of its candidates would still contest the election on
the SNS electoral list.^[301] <#cite_note-302> Individuals who were
formerly critical of SNS and Vučić, including Tatjana Macura <https://
en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tatjana_Macura>, formerly aligned with DJB and now
a co-president of Party of Modern Serbia <https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/
Party_of_Modern_Serbia>, Radoslav Milojičić <https://en.wikipedia.org/
wiki/Radoslav_Miloji%C4%8Di%C4%87>, formerly aligned with DS and now the
president of Serbian Left <https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/
Serbian_Left_(2022)>, and Dejan Bulatović <https://en.wikipedia.org/
wiki/Dejan_Bulatovi%C4%87>, formerly aligned with SSP and now the
president of Alliance of Social Democrats, were all announced as
candidates of the SNS electoral list for the 2023 election.^[302]
<#cite_note-303>

Despite no longer being president of SNS, but still serving as president
of Serbia, Vučić has been the main representative of SNS in the election
campaign.^[303] <#cite_note-304> ^[304] <#cite_note-305> Vučić himself
is also not a candidate in any elections.^[305] <#cite_note-306> Vučić
has strongly criticised the opposition, saying that "every vote for the
opposition is a vote for the president of the Party of Freedom and
Justice, Dragan Đilas <https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dragan_%C4%90ilas>,
a vote for the independence of Kosovo, and for the introduction of
sanctions to Russia".^[306] <#cite_note-:54-307> Despite not being
affiliated with SPN, Vučić has also alleged that "when people vote for
[Boško] Obradović and [Miloš] Jovanović, they know that they are voting
for Đilas, Dragan Šolak <https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/
Dragan_%C5%A0olak_(businessman)> and all of them".^[306] <#cite_note-:
54-307> Vučić has also portrayed the election as "between the past, the
parties of the former regime that would return [Serbia] to the past, and
the future".^[307] <#cite_note-308> In an interview, Vučić alleged that
"there is a plan of foreign governments to overthrow SNS"; Vučević
alleged the same.^[308] <#cite_note-309> ^[309] <#cite_note-310> Vučić
has also alleged that the entire opposition is controlled by
Đilas.^[310] <#cite_note-311> Minister Aleksandar Martinović <https://
en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aleksandar_Martinovi%C4%87> also alleged that the
"opposition wants to provoke a civil war", while Brnabić said that "the
goal of the opposition is to create chaos and demonstrations after 17
December".^[311] <#cite_note-312> ^[312] <#cite_note-313> CRTA
criticised the statements of Martinović and Brnabić, saying that "in
order to calm tensions in the public, intimidating citizens and
encouraging an atmosphere of fear in the election campaign should
stop".^[313] <#cite_note-314> Opposition figures such as Lazović,
Obradović, and Jovanović also condemned the statements of Martinović and
Brnabić.^[314] <#cite_note-315>

Vučić announced on 29 October that the government of Serbia would by 1
December payout DIN <https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Serbian_dinar> 10,000
to beneficiaries of social assistance, of which there are 170,000 in
Serbia, to blind, demented, and elderly persons, of which there are
51,000, and that students would receive discounts on train and plane
tickets.^[315] <#cite_note-316> Despite the government denying that this
decision would influence the voters, Nemanja Nenadić, from non-profit
organisation Transparency Serbia <https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/
Transparency_Serbia>, listed the payouts and discounts as "one of the
ways to subtly influence the will of the citizens, to make them think
that the government makes concessions to them".^[316] <#cite_note-317>
In response to Vučić's campaign, DS submitted a report to the Anti-
Corruption Agency, alleging that Vučić is leading the SNS campaign
despite being only head of state and that Vučić is allegedly abusing
power to boost SNS in the elections.^[317] <#cite_note-:62-318> The
Bureau of Social Research (BIRODI) also claimed that Vučić violated
Article 40 of the Law on Prevention of Corruption.^[317] <#cite_note-:
62-318> Zoran Čvorović, a professor at the Faculty of Law <https://
en.wikipedia.org/wiki/University_of_Belgrade_Faculty_of_Law>, argued
that as president of Serbia, Vučić violated the constitution due to him
being listed as the representatives of all SNS-led lists in the 2023
elections.^[318] <#cite_note-319> RIK rejected all 15 citizens'
complaints related to Vučić being listed in the name of the SNS-led
electoral list, despite not taking part in the elections, saying that
"Vučić has agreed on paper for his name to be mentioned on the electoral
list".^[319] <#cite_note-320> The government of Serbia introduced more
populist measures in late November, such as DIN <https://
en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Serbian_dinar> 10,000 payouts to high school
students.^[320] <#cite_note-321>

SNS began collecting signatures for its electoral list on 1
November.^[321] <#cite_note-322> According to media reports, SNS
collected over 83,000 signatures by the end of the day.^[322]
<#cite_note-323> SNS submitted its list to RIK a day later, with 92,637
signatures in total.^[323] <#cite_note-324> RIK confirmed its list on 3
November with 88,083 valid signatures collected.^[218] <#cite_note-
RIK_SNS-218> Vučić and SNS held a campaign meeting in Leskovac on 5
November, at which Vučić promised to raise salaries while also
criticising the SPN alliance.^[324] <#cite_note-325> ^[325]
<#cite_note-326> Orlić and Nevena Đurić <https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/
Nevena_%C4%90uri%C4%87>, vice-presidents of SNS, campaigned in Ruma
<https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ruma>, where they pledged citizens more
investments in infrastructure, education, and technology.^[326]
<#cite_note-327> Another campaign meeting was held on 9 November in
Pirot <https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pirot>, featuring Vučić, Brnabić,
Vučević, Stamatović, and PUPS leader Milan Krkobabić <https://
en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Milan_Krkobabi%C4%87> as speakers.^[327]
<#cite_note-328> At a campaign rally in Smederevo <https://
en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Smederevo>, Vučić said that "if the opposition
wins in the next election, I will resign as president of Serbia".^[328]
<#cite_note-329> SNS has also campaigned on improving the status of
women and introducing more mammograms <https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/
Mammogram> in Serbian hospitals.^[329] <#cite_note-330> ^[330]
<#cite_note-331> SNS has also expressed its support for the accession of
Serbia to the European Union.^[331] <#cite_note-:45-332> Nikolić made
his first public appearance since 2017 at the SNS convention in Belgrade
on 2 December.^[332] <#cite_note-333> At the conference, Aleksandar "Aca
Rošavi" Vidojević, a close associate of convicted criminal Veljko
Belivuk, was also present.^[333] <#cite_note-334> SNS held its last
convention in Novi Sad on 13 December.^[334] <#cite_note-335>


SPS, JS, and ZS signed a cooperation agreement on 1 November, officially
announcing that they would contest the elections together under the same
electoral list name, "Ivica Dačić – Prime Minister of Serbia", that they
contested in the 2022 parliamentary election.^[335] <#cite_note-:
112-336> The SPS-led coalition submitted its list to RIK on 2 November,
with more than 20,000 signatures.^[336] <#cite_note-337> RIK confirmed
their list on 4 November with 19,618 valid signatures in total.^[219]
<#cite_note-RIK_SPS-219> Boban Stojanović said that RIK should have
rejected the SPS electoral list because a number of signatures of
support were certified by notaries who do not exist in the notaries
database.^[337] <#cite_note-338> People's Party of Srpska, a political
party in Republika Srpska <https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/
Republika_Srpska>, expressed their support for SPS in November
2023.^[338] <#cite_note-339>

Despite being a coalition government partner with SNS since 2012, SPS
official Dušan Bajatović <https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/
Du%C5%A1an_Bajatovi%C4%87> has been a target of attacks in articles
published by pro-government media.^[339] <#cite_note-340> During the
campaign period, SPS has presented themselves as "guarantees of
political stability" while they also expressed their support for youth
rights and youth activism.^[340] <#cite_note-341> ^[341]
<#cite_note-342> Dačić has also tried to portray the coalition as
socialist; while campaigning in Ljubovija <https://en.wikipedia.org/
wiki/Ljubovija>, Dačić said that "by voting for the list Ivica Dačić –
Prime Minister of Serbia, you are also voting for patriotism and
socialism".^[342] <#cite_note-343> While campaigning in Mrčajevci
<https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mr%C4%8Dajevci>, Dačić also said that the
SPS coalition supports free education, free universal health care, and
social funds.^[343] <#cite_note-344> Dačić also reflected on his
opinions about Milošević during the campaign, saying that "Milošević was
an example of how to love and defend your country".^[344]
<#cite_note-345> The SPS coalition has also expressed its support for
the accession of Serbia to the European Union.^[331] <#cite_note-:45-332>


        Serbia Against Violence

Serbia Against Violence convention in Belgrade on 12 December 2023
<https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/
File:Serbia_Against_Violence_convention_in_Belgrade,_12_December_2023_(4)_(cropped).jpg>
SPN has campaigned on increasing pensions, salaries, and investing in
education and universal health care

Members of the SPN coalition, with the addition of Romanian Party and
the Civic Democratic Party, signed a cooperation agreement on 3
November, saying that "fight against crime and corruption, stopping
inflation and the impoverishment of citizens, restoring pensions reduced
in 2014, and the importance of security, especially for the youngest"
will be their main issues during the campaign.^[345] <#cite_note-346>
SPN submitted its list to RIK on 8 November.^[346] <#cite_note-347>
Their electoral list was confirmed by RIK on 9 November.^[224]
<#cite_note-RIK_SPN-224> While the negotiations were still ongoing,
Lutovac listed Gordana Matković <https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/
Gordana_Matkovi%C4%87>, a minister under the governments of Zoran Đinđić
<https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zoran_%C4%90in%C4%91i%C4%87> and Zoran
Živković <https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/
Zoran_%C5%BDivkovi%C4%87_(politician)>, and Ivan Vujačić <https://
en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?
title=Ivan_Vuja%C4%8Di%C4%87&action=edit&redlink=1> [sr <https://
sr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ivan_Vuja%C4%8Di%C4%87>], former leader of DS in
the National Assembly, as two potential candidates for the position of
prime minister, saying that they are "strong and accomplished
personalities, they have rich professional and political experience,
their public interest is above party or personal interest".^[347]
<#cite_note-348> SPN, however, decided to present Tepić and Aleksić as
their two main representatives.^[194] <#cite_note-:39-194>

Before and during the official campaign period, politicians affiliated
with SPN, including Tepić, Aleksić, Ćuta, and Srđan Milivojević
<https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sr%C4%91an_Milivojevi%C4%87>, a DS member
of the National Assembly, were featured on propaganda flyers that were
spread in Novi Sad and Belgrade, depicting them in a negative
matter.^[348] <#cite_note-:210-349> ^[349] <#cite_note-350> Pavle
Grbović <https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pavle_Grbovi%C4%87>, the
president of PSG, was also featured on posters that depicted him as an
Ustaša <https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Usta%C5%A1a>.^[350]
<#cite_note-351> The posters that featured Grbović were promoted by
Đorđe Dabić <https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/%C4%90or%C4%91e_Dabi%C4%87>,
a SNS state secretary.^[348] <#cite_note-:210-349> Aleksić accused Vučić
of being behind these ideas, while Grbović filed complaints about the
posters.^[351] <#cite_note-352> ^[352] <#cite_note-353> Janko
Veselinović <https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/
Janko_Veselinovi%C4%87_(lawyer)>, the leader of the Movement for
Reversal <https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Movement_for_Reversal>, was
physically assaulted in Novi Sad on 12 November.^[353] <#cite_note-354>
Attacks on SSP offices on Zvezdara <https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/
Zvezdara>, a Belgrade municipality, were conducted on 16 November.^[354]
<#cite_note-355>

SPN has campaigned on returning "stolen pensions", the pensions that
were lowered by Vučić's government in 2014, and on environmental
issues.^[355] <#cite_note-356> ^[356] <#cite_note-:35-357> Ćuta
highlighted the issue of poverty and hunger.^[356] <#cite_note-:35-357>
Lazović has also said that SPN supports removing national broadcast
frequency status for Happy <https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/
Nacionalna_Televizija_Happy> and Pink <https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/
Pink_(Serbia)> television channels, lowing the inflation and prices, and
investing in universal health care protection <https://en.wikipedia.org/
wiki/Universal_health_care>.^[357] <#cite_note-:63-358> Aleksić added
that SPN would introduce progressive taxation <https://en.wikipedia.org/
wiki/Progressive_taxation>, while Đilas said that SPN would also
increase salaries and invest in education.^[357] <#cite_note-:63-358>
^[358] <#cite_note-:55-359> Attended by several thousand supporters, SPN
held its last campaign convention on 12 December in Belgrade.^[359]
<#cite_note-360>


        National Democratic Alternative

NADA began its official campaign on 28 October, listing corruption,
nepotism, party employment, and rejecting Ohrid Agreement as one of its
main issues for the election.^[360] <#cite_note-361> NADA submitted its
list to RIK on 6 November and RIK confirmed it a day later.^[252]
<#cite_note-:32-253> ^[222] <#cite_note-RIK_NADA-222> Shortly before the
beginning of the official campaign period, Jovanović was featured on
propaganda posters in October 2023, falsely depicting him as someone who
freed incumbent prime minister of Kosovo, Albin Kurti, in 2001.^[348]
<#cite_note-:210-349> Several NADA billboard posters were later torn
down on 21 November; NADA accused the government of being behind the
acts.^[361] <#cite_note-362>

During the campaign period, Jovanović intensified his criticism of SNS
while declining to criticise pro-European parties.^[362] <#cite_note-:
110-363> He has also called for greater cooperation between opposition
parties to topple SNS from power.^[363] <#cite_note-364> Jovanović has
called for electoral reform, pledging to "destroy the partocracy
<https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Partocracy> that SNS created".^[362]
<#cite_note-:110-363> Jovanović said that NADA wants to introduce the
first-past-the-post system <https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/First-past-
the-post_voting>, claiming that with the introduction with a such system
"the possibility of the existence of a party state would be
destroyed".^[364] <#cite_note-365> NADA has also campaigned on further
regionalisation <https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Regionalism_(politics)>
and decentralisation of Serbia and giving cities and municipalities more
power in regards to infrastructure and economy.^[365] <#cite_note-366>
Jovanović has also called for the reform of healthcare and agriculture,
saying that "an incredible sum from the budget goes into private
pockets, through the purchase of expensive medicines and medical
equipment" and that "agriculture should be a strategic branch of the
economy and accordingly the state must improve working conditions for
farmers".^[366] <#cite_note-367> ^[367] <#cite_note-368> Vojislav
Mihailović of POKS also called for the restoration of the monarchy,
saying that "Serbia should be a constitutional, parliamentary monarchy
like organised European countries".^[368] <#cite_note-369>

Regarding foreign policy, NADA has campaigned on wanting "the best
possible cooperation with the European Union" in regards to trade,
economy, and culture.^[369] <#cite_note-:40-370> It has hower expressed
its opposition to Serbia joining the European Union due to "the
condition set for Serbia to recognise the secession of Kosovo".^[369]
<#cite_note-:40-370> NADA held its last campaign convention on 10
December.^[370] <#cite_note-371>


        National Gathering

Milica Đurđević Stamenkovski, Boško Obradović, and ten other Dveri and
SSZ politicians giving a press conference at the Republic Electoral
Commission on 4 November 2023 <https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/
File:Milica_%C4%90ur%C4%91evi%C4%87_Stamenkovski_and_Bo%C5%A1ko_Obradovi%C4%87_at_RIK,_4_November_2023.png>
The SSZ–Dveri coalition has campaigned on forging closer relations with
BRICS <https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/BRICS>, instead of the European
Union, and opposing the implementation of the Ohrid Agreement <https://
en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ohrid_Agreement_(2023)>

SSZ and Dveri, the members of the NO coalition, signed another
cooperation agreement on 1 November, announcing that they would
officially contest the elections together.^[371] <#cite_note-:31-372>
Obradović named preserving traditional values and Kosovo as part of
Serbia, supporting Republika Srpska, Serbs in neighbouring regions, and
ecological patriotism <https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eco-nationalism> as
one of their main issues.^[371] <#cite_note-:31-372> The coalition
submitted its list on 4 November and it was accepted by RIK a day
later.^[221] <#cite_note-NO_RIK-221> ^[372] <#cite_note-373> At a press
conference after they presented their electoral list, Đurđević
Stamenkovski emphasised their opposition to the Ohrid Agreement and the
European Union.^[373] <#cite_note-374> The far-right Alternative for
Germany <https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alternative_for_Germany> party,
the Ravna Gora Movement, and the clerical-fascist Obraz <https://
en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Obraz_(organization)> organisation of Mladen
Obradović, voiced their support for the SSZ–Dveri coalition.^[374]
<#cite_note-:232-375> ^[375] <#cite_note-376> ^[376] <#cite_note-377>

During the campaign period, the SSZ–Dveri coalition representatives
emphasised their support for greater incentives for domestic businessmen
and farmers,^[377] <#cite_note-378> the construction of student
dormitories in Belgrade, Novi Sad, Niš and Kragujevac, giving free
school books, and financial aid for "socially vulnerable
families".^[378] <#cite_note-379> ^[379] <#cite_note-380> Ratko Ristić
<https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?
title=Ratko_Risti%C4%87&action=edit&redlink=1>, one of the
representatives of the NO coalition, also said that one of their main
issues is to "return Serbia's sovereignty, especially economic
sovereignty" and that they would "pay special attention to the
development of Serbian agriculture and the position of Serbian
farmers".^[380] <#cite_note-381> Đurđević Stamenkovski also said that
she wants Serbia to return "the proven traditional values in the
education system".^[381] <#cite_note-382> Obradović alleged that the
SSZ–Dveri coalition was a target of attacks and media censorship.^[382]
<#cite_note-383>

On foreign policy, the coalition expressed their support for retaining
close relations with China, due to their positions towards Kosovo,^[383]
<#cite_note-384> and that they would "request that Serbia become a part
of BRICS <https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/BRICS>", saying that BRICS is an
alternative to the European Union.^[384] <#cite_note-385> Ivan Kostić
<https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ivan_Kosti%C4%87_(Serbian_politician)> of
Dveri also said that "cooperation with BRICS would have better effects
on the Serbian economy" than with the European Union.^[385]
<#cite_note-386> Obradović alleged that regions such as Sandžak
<https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sand%C5%BEak>, Vojvodina <https://
en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vojvodina>, and parts of eastern Serbia would
separate from Serbia if "Serbia gives up on Kosovo".^[386]
<#cite_note-387> Đurđević Stamenkovski, in an Insajder interview, did
not reject cooperating with SNS after the elections if SNS rejects the
Ohrid Agreement.^[387] <#cite_note-388> NO held its last campaign
convention on 10 December.^[388] <#cite_note-389>


        Serbian Radical Party

SRS presented its electoral list to RIK on 3 November RIK confirmed it a
day later.^[389] <#cite_note-390> ^[390] <#cite_note-391> SRS has
campaigned on issues such as health care reform, saying that Serbia
should "use the experiences of foreign, Western European countries, as
well as the USA, which has a more developed health system",^[391]
<#cite_note-392> advocating greater investments for domestic companies,
and preventing bullying by creating "teams of parents, educators, and
local municipal officers".^[392] <#cite_note-393> ^[393]
<#cite_note-394> Aleksandar Šešelj <https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/
Aleksandar_%C5%A0e%C5%A1elj> has also said that SRS supports a ban on
non-governmental organisations that support the recognition of
Kosovo.^[394] <#cite_note-395>

In an interview for Radio Television of Vojvodina <https://
en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Radio_Television_of_Vojvodina>, Aleksandar Šešelj
said that SRS would not join a pro-European government in case if SRS
crosses the electoral threshold.^[395] <#cite_note-396> SRS has called
for the abandonment of the process of accession of Serbia to the
European Union and instead called on forging closer ties with Russia and
becoming an applicant member of BRICS.^[396] <#cite_note-397> Vojislav
Šešelj also met with the Palestinian ambassador in Serbia during the
campaign; Vojislav Šešelj also criticised Israel, describing their
actions towards Palestine <https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/
State_of_Palestine> as genocidal <https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/
Palestinian_genocide_accusation>.^[397] <#cite_note-398> ^[398]
<#cite_note-399>


        Alliance of Vojvodina Hungarians

VMSZ, led by acting president Bálint Pásztor <https://en.wikipedia.org/
wiki/B%C3%A1lint_P%C3%A1sztor>, submitted its list to RIK on 7
November.^[251] <#cite_note-VMSZ_slogan-252> At a press conference after
submitting the list, Pásztor said that VMSZ collected 11,355 signatures,
more than twice the amount needed for minority parties, and that they
would campaign on issues they issued in their electoral programme.^[251]
<#cite_note-VMSZ_slogan-252> RIK confirmed their list on 8
November.^[223] <#cite_note-RIK_VMSZ-223> Pásztor expressed his support
for continuing the cooperation between VMSZ and SNS.^[399]
<#cite_note-400> VMSZ received support from the Democratic Party of
Vojvodina Hungarians <https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/
Democratic_Party_of_Vojvodina_Hungarians> and Party of Hungarian Unity
in late November.^[400] <#cite_note-401>


        United for Justice

SPP and DSHV formalised an electoral alliance under the name United for
Justice (UZP) on 4 November.^[401] <#cite_note-402> UZP submitted its
list to RIK on 9 November, with Zukorlić stating that the coalition
would advocate for proportional representation of national communities
in public institutions and balanced regional development.^[402]
<#cite_note-403> Their electoral list was accepted by RIK on 10
November.^[225] <#cite_note-RIK_UZP-225> UZP members expressed their
support for remaining in the next government, saying "that members of
our communities supported this move".^[403] <#cite_note-404> Zukorlić
has described UZP as a pro-European coalition and has also said that "he
believes that one day Serbia will nevertheless join the NATO
alliance".^[404] <#cite_note-405> DSHV received support from Andrej
Plenković <https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Andrej_Plenkovi%C4%87>, the
prime minister of Croatia and leader of the Croatian Democratic Union
<https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Croatian_Democratic_Union>.^[405]
<#cite_note-406>


        Party of Democratic Action of Sandžak

SDAS of Sulejman Ugljanin <https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/
Sulejman_Ugljanin> submitted its electoral list to RIK on 16 November,
with RIK confirming it on the same day.^[226] <#cite_note-RIK_SDAS-226>
^[406] <#cite_note-:34-407> Its main representative and ballot holder,
Selma Kučević <https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Selma_Ku%C4%8Devi%C4%87>,
emphasised that SDAS supports decentralisation and regionalism as well
as "authentically representing the Bosniak people as well as other
citizens of Sandžak".^[406] <#cite_note-:34-407> Ugljanin has said that
SDAS supports anti-corruption measures and government
transparency.^[407] <#cite_note-408>


        Coalition for Peace and Tolerance

A group of ethnic minority parties and organisations, including Vlach
National Party <https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vlach_National_Party>
(VNS), Hungarian Civic Alliance <https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/
Hungarian_Civic_Alliance_(Serbia)> (MPSZ), and Democratic Party of
Macedonians <https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/
Democratic_Party_of_Macedonians>, held a meeting in April 2023, with the
intention being on forming a coalition, named Coalition for Peace and
Tolerance <https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/
Coalition_for_Peace_and_Tolerance>, for the upcoming parliamentary,
provincial, and local elections.^[408] <#cite_note-409> Shortly after
the meeting, Jahja Fehratović <https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/
Jahja_Fehratovi%C4%87> left SPP.^[409] <#cite_note-410> Later in
October, Fehratović announced the formation of his political party, the
For the Future and Development <https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?
title=For_the_Future_and_Development&action=edit&redlink=1> (ZBR).^[410]
<#cite_note-:36-411> Fehratović said that ZBR would support traditional
values, spirituality, and rule of law.^[410] <#cite_note-:36-411>

Following the dissolution of the National Assembly, Fehratović's ZBR
formed a coalition, named "Together for the Future and Development –
Coalition for Peace and Development" (KZMT), with VNS, MPSZ, Democratic
Union of Croats <https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/
Democratic_Union_of_Croats>, Bosniak Civic Party, Party of Montenegrins,
Civic Party of Greeks of Serbia, Vojvodina Movement, Tolerance of
Serbia, Union of Yugoslavs, Union of Female Roma Network and Non-Roma
Network of Serbia, and Union of Banat Romanians.^[411] <#cite_note-:
37-412> Fehratović was also announced as the coalition's ballot
holder.^[411] <#cite_note-:37-412> KZMT submitted its electoral list on
17 November.^[412] <#cite_note-413> RIK rejected the list on 18
November, stating that out of 6,093 collected signatures, only 4,937 are
valid, and that KZMT must collect the remaining 63 signatures until 20
November.^[413] <#cite_note-414> On the same day, KZMT collected 436
more valid signatures and RIK confirmed their electoral list.^[227]
<#cite_note-RIK_KZMT-227>


        People's Party

After collecting more than 12,500 signatures, Narodna submitted its
electoral list to RIK on 19 November.^[414] <#cite_note-:38-415> At a
press conference in the building of RIK, Jeremić said that Narodna would
campaign on rejecting the Ohrid Agreement, prohibiting lithium mining
<https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lithium_mining>, as well as "bringing
back sovereignty over the national economy".^[414] <#cite_note-:38-415>
RIK confirmed their electoral list on 20 November.^[228] <#cite_note-
RIK_NARODNA-228>

Narodna has also emphasised its support for introducing military
conscription <https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Military_conscription> to
retain military neutrality, retaining close relations with Russia, and
opposing sanctions against Russia, the accession of Serbia to the
European Union, and the recognition of Kosovo.^[415] <#cite_note-416>
Jeremić has said that Serbia should seek membership in the European
Economic Area <https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/European_Economic_Area>
instead.^[416] <#cite_note-417>


        DJB–SDS

Initially, SDS was supposed to take part in the SPN alliance while DJB
announced that they would contest the elections independently.^[417]
<#cite_note-418> SDS was ultimately declined to join SPN, and shortly
after in early November, DJB successfully negotiated with SDS and Ana
Pejić's Stolen Babies movement to form a joint electoral alliance,
mainly centering their opposition to the Ohrid Agreement.^[418]
<#cite_note-419> ^[419] <#cite_note-420> The coalition, named Good
Morning Serbia, submitted its electoral list to RIK on 22
November.^[420] <#cite_note-421> They collected over 11,500 signatures
of support.^[421] <#cite_note-422> RIK confirmed their electoral list on
23 November, with 10,534 valid signatures.^[229] <#cite_note-RIK_DJS-229>


        Others

The Russian Party, together with the New Communist Party of Yugoslavia
<https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_Communist_Party_of_Yugoslavia>
(NKPJ), submitted its electoral list on 25 November.^[422]
<#cite_note-423> On the same day, the Liberal Democratic Party <https://
en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Liberal_Democratic_Party_(Serbia)> (LDP) of
Čedomir Jovanović <https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/
%C4%8Cedomir_Jovanovi%C4%87> and the Serbia in the West coalition,
composed of Nova–D2SP, Civic Democratic Forum <https://en.wikipedia.org/
wiki/Civic_Democratic_Forum>, Liberals and Democrats, and Glas submitted
their electoral list.^[423] <#cite_note-424> ^[424] <#cite_note-425>
^[425] <#cite_note-426> The electoral lists of the citizens group We–The
Voice from the People (MI–GIN), represented by conspiracy theorist
Branimir Nestorović <https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/
Branimir_Nestorovi%C4%87>.^[426] <#cite_note-427> ^[427]
<#cite_note-428> RIK proclaimed the electoral lists of We–The Voice from
the People and Serbia in the West on 27 November.^[231] <#cite_note-
RIK_27Nov-231> On 28 November, the electoral lists of Russian Party–NKPJ
and LDP were proclaimed by RIK.^[232] <#cite_note-RIK_RSLDP-232>
Jovanović met with Kurti on 3 December, with whom he discussed about
Serbia–Kosovo relations.^[428] <#cite_note-429>


    Opinion polls

Opinion polling <https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Opinion_polling> for the
2023 parliamentary election in Serbia was conducted by various
monitoring and research organisations such as Demostat, NSPM, Agency
Faktor Plus, Šta Srbija misli?/New Third Way, Stata Agency, and
CRTA.^[429] <#cite_note-430> Stata Agency has also published scenario
polls, featuring a SNS–SPS alliance, the Serbia Against Violence
coalition, and the "state-building opposition"; Vukadinović of NSPM has
criticised Stata's scenario polls, saying that the coalition "Serbia
Against Violence is not exactly a fiction, then, for now, only a
projection and, possibly, the desire of some media and political
factors. It is difficult to compare something that actually exists with
something that could possibly be".^[430] <#cite_note-:23-431> Anđelković
also said that "public's pulse is very fluid when the elections are
still relatively far away".^[430] <#cite_note-:23-431> Besides Stata,
CRTA has also published a scenario poll in October 2023.^[431]
<#cite_note-432>

The Bureau of Social Research (BIRODI) has criticised opinion polling in
which "information about the name of the agency that conducted the
opinion poll, the individual who ordered the opinion poll, the number of
respondents, the time when the opinion poll was carried out, as well as
the question that were asked to the respondents" is not present, and has
called news agencies to not publish those opinion polls.^[432]
<#cite_note-:24-433> BIRODI has stated these organisations "give the
opportunity to use opinion polls for propaganda purposes" and has noted
that the elements lead to the "deprofessionalisation of a public opinion
researcher".^[432] <#cite_note-:24-433> Srećko Mihailović of Demostat
has also stated that most opinion polls in Serbia are "biased and
unprofessional", claiming that "clients are political parties and the
government, and researchers manipulate the ratings of parties" in
opinion polls.^[433] <#cite_note-434> The World Association for Public
Opinion Research <https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/
World_Association_for_Public_Opinion_Research>, an international
professional association of opinion poll researchers, has listed Serbia
as a country where there is a denial of the right to public opinion
research, stating that "there is pressure from the government,
politicians, and some media".^[434] <#cite_note-435>


      Graphical summary

The graph below showcases major parties and alliances in opinion polls
from the 2022 parliamentary election to 17 December 2023.

    Conduct

On election day, 17 December, voting stations were opened from 07:00 to
20:00.^[435] <#cite_note-RIK_rokovi-436> Monitoring and non-governmental
organisations, such as CeSID <https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/CeSID>,
CRTA, and Kreni-Promeni, reported that the election day was marked with
electoral fraud <https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Electoral_fraud>.^[436]
<#cite_note-:48-437> ^[437] <#cite_note-:58-438> ^[438] <#cite_note-439>
^[439] <#cite_note-440> By 9:00, CeSID reported over 50 irregularities,
this included irregularities such as non-compliance of procedures by
members of election committees and voters photographing or recording
their ballot papers, while Kreni-Promeni reported instances of
irregularities, including the Bulgarian train <https://en.wikipedia.org/
wiki/Bulgarian_train> vote-rigging method at voting stations in New
Belgrade <https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_Belgrade>.^[436]
<#cite_note-:48-437> Nedeljkov from CRTA also reported that in Odžaci
<https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Od%C5%BEaci> CRTA observers were
physically attacked and that their cars sustained damage from the
attackers.^[440] <#cite_note-:49-441> In Odžaci, CRTA observers
previously reported an instance of a Bulgarian train.^[440]
<#cite_note-:49-441> Throughout the rest of the election day, CeSID
continued to report more irregularities and intimidation.^[441]
<#cite_note-442> Parandilović from SPN also published a video in which
two Priboj <https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Priboj> councillor candidates
were rigging election ballots.^[442] <#cite_note-443>

Voters from Republika Srpska <https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/
Republika_Srpska> were also driven to the Štark Arena <https://
en.wikipedia.org/wiki/%C5%A0tark_Arena> in Belgrade.^[443]
<#cite_note-444> Despite Štark Arena not being a voting station, voters
from Republika Srpska confirmed that the Arena was used illegally as a
voting station and as a redirect station towards official voting
stations in Belgrade.^[444] <#cite_note-445> The security at the Štark
Arena did not allow members of RIK to enter the building.^[445]
<#cite_note-446> Brnabić said that she did not see what was irregular or
illegal with the arena serving as a redirect station for voters from
Republika Srpska.^[446] <#cite_note-447> Miodrag Jovanović, a professor
at the Faculty of Law, said that in regards to the Arena, "it is illegal
for someone to have a residence where he does not live".^[447]
<#cite_note-448>

In its report, ODIHR concluded that SNS had a "systematic advantage
which created unfair conditions in the elections" and that Vučić, the
president of Serbia, heavily dominated the election campaign, despite
not being a candidate in it.^[448] <#cite_note-:57-449> According to
ODIHR, there was abuse of public funds, the media monitoring body,
Regulatory Body for Electronic Media, was also not efficient during the
election campaign, and that despite the elections being well organised,
they were organised in a "societal and political divided
ambience".^[448] <#cite_note-:57-449> ODIHR said that the campaign was
polarised and met with negative campaigning and fearmongering <https://
en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fearmongering>.^[448] <#cite_note-:57-449> The
Federal Foreign Office <https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/
Federal_Foreign_Office> of Germany said that abuse of public funds,
fearmongering of voters, and vote buying is "unacceptable for a country
with the status of a candidate for EU membership".^[449] <#cite_note-450>

Stefan Schennach <https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?
title=Stefan_Schennach&action=edit&redlink=1> [de <https://
de.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stefan_Schennach>], the chief of the delegation of
PACE that monitored the elections, said that "the elections were not
fair" and that he had seen "ballots that were printed by a
photocopier".^[450] <#cite_note-451> In a joint statement, Josep Borrell
<https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Josep_Borrell> and Olivér Várhelyi
<https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oliv%C3%A9r_V%C3%A1rhelyi>, on behalf of
the European Commission, said that Serbia's "electoral process requires
tangible improvement and further reform".^[451] <#cite_note-452>
Political scientist Florian Bieber <https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/
Florian_Bieber> said that "irregularities appeared to be more widespread
than in previous [elections]".^[452] <#cite_note-453> Matthew Miller
<https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Matthew_Miller_(spokesperson)>, the
spokesperson of the United States Department of State <https://
en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Department_of_State>, called for the
government of Serbia to investigate the irregularities that
occurred.^[453] <#cite_note-454> United States senators Jeanne Shaheen
<https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jeanne_Shaheen> and Pete Ricketts
<https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pete_Ricketts> also called for the
government to "urgently consider whether elections should be repeated in
certain regions", saying that the elections were not free and
fair.^[454] <#cite_note-455> Andreas Schieder <https://en.wikipedia.org/
wiki/Andreas_Schieder>, who monitored the elections on behalf of the
European Parliament, criticised Brnabić, saying that "the government
should work on solving numerous claims about pressure on voters, vote
buying, violating voting secrecy, biased media, and the president's
involvement in the campaign".^[455] <#cite_note-456>

Vučić and SNS denied all of the electoral fraud allegations.^[437]
<#cite_note-:58-438> Brnabić accused the opposition and CRTA of
"destabilising Serbia and its constitutional order" and verbally
attacked Schennach and Schieder due to them criticising the conduct of
the election.^[456] <#cite_note-457> ^[457] <#cite_note-458>


    Results

There were 6,500,666 citizens in total who had the right to vote in the
parliamentary election.^[458] <#cite_note-459> Out of 8,273 voting
stations in total, voters abroad could have voted at 81 voting stations
in 35 different countries.^[459] <#cite_note-:41-460> ^[460]
<#cite_note-461> 32,216 dual citizens registered to take part in the
elections abroad.^[459] <#cite_note-:41-460> In Canada, Portugal, the
United Kingdom, and the United States, voting occurred on 16 December
from 07:00 to 20:00.^[231] <#cite_note-RIK_27Nov-231> Elections will be
repeated at 30 voting stations in 19 different municipalities on 30
December.^[461] <#cite_note-462>

After the voting stations were closed, CeSID/Ipsos and CRTA were the
first to report their projections of the results.^[462] <#cite_note-463>
^[463] <#cite_note-464> According to the 18 December projection from
CeSID/Ipsos, SNS won 46 percent of popular vote and 128 seats in the
National Assembly, successfully returning its parliamentary majority,
while SPN placed second, with 23.6 percent of popular vote and 65 seats
in the National Assembly.^[464] <#cite_note-:50-465> According to CeSID/
Ipsos, SPS only won 6 percent of popular vote and 18 seats in the
National Assembly, this being the worst result of SPS since the 2007
parliamentary election <https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/
2007_Serbian_parliamentary_election>, while NADA won 4.9 percent of
popular vote.^[464] <#cite_note-:50-465> In a surprise move,
Nestorović's MI–GIN also crossed the threshold, winning 13 seats in
total.^[464] <#cite_note-:50-465> Out of the minority lists, VMSZ won 6
seats, SPP–DSHV won 3 seats, SDAS won 2 seats, and SDAS and Russian
Party won one seat respectively.^[464] <#cite_note-:50-465> The NO
coalition of Dveri and SSZ failed to cross the threshold, winning only
2.8 percent of popular vote.^[465] <#cite_note-466> SNS received the
most votes abroad.^[466] <#cite_note-467>

RIK broadcast the results live, with the results being updated every 5
minutes.^[467] <#cite_note-468> After the publishing of the overall
report on the election, RIK must award the candidates the seats of the
National Assembly in less than 10 days.^[435] <#cite_note-RIK_rokovi-436>

    Aftermath

The Economist Intelligence Unit <https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/
Economist_Intelligence_Unit> (EIU) and /Danas/ newspaper reported in
early December that on 22 September, Vučić signed an agreement with the
European Commission <https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/European_Commission>
on the production of lithium batteries in Serbia.^[470] <#cite_note-:
47-471> The government of Serbia previously cancelled the Rio Tinto
<https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rio_Tinto_(corporation)> lithium mine
project in January 2022, amidst the environmental protests <https://
en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2021%E2%80%932022_Serbian_environmental_protests>,
but the EIU reported that in the September 2023 agreement "the
government [of Serbia] has not given up on a plan to allow the mining of
lithium at Jadar".^[470] <#cite_note-:47-471> The agreement also
includes a construction of another factory in Ćuprija <https://
en.wikipedia.org/wiki/%C4%86uprija>.^[470] <#cite_note-:47-471> EIU
stated that due to the 2023 parliamentary election, "the government is
likely to stall the plans, reviving them only once the December election
is over".^[470] <#cite_note-:47-471>

Following the elections on 17 December, SPN began organising protests
outside the RIK building.^[471] <#cite_note-472> At the 18 December
protest, Aleksić and Tepić announced that they would go on a hunger
strike <https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hunger_strike> until the results
of the Belgrade City Assembly elections are annulled.^[472]
<#cite_note-473> SPN expanded their demands on 20 December by demanding
the annulment of all 17 December election results.^[473]
<#cite_note-474> Alongside SPN, NADA, Narodna, SDS, and Dveri also
expressed their support for the annulment of 17 December election
results and the scheduling of a new ones.^[474] <#cite_note-475> On 21
December, members of the National Assembly Jelena Milošević <https://
en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?
title=Jelena_Milo%C5%A1evi%C4%87&action=edit&redlink=1> and Danijela
Grujić <https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?
title=Danijela_Gruji%C4%87&action=edit&redlink=1> joined Aleksić and
Tepić in their hunger strike.^[475] <#cite_note-476> A day later, Janko
Veselinović <https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/
Janko_Veselinovi%C4%87_(lawyer)> and Željko Veselinović <https://
en.wikipedia.org/wiki/%C5%BDeljko_Veselinovi%C4%87> also began their
hunger strike, while on 23 December MPs-elect Branko Miljuš <https://
en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?
title=Branko_Milju%C5%A1_(politician)&action=edit&redlink=1> and Dušan
Nikezić <https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?
title=Du%C5%A1an_Nikezi%C4%87&action=edit&redlink=1> began their hunger
strike.^[476] <#cite_note-477> ^[477] <#cite_note-478>

Due to failing to cross the threshold, Obradović of Dveri and all
members of the presidency of Narodna, including president Jeremić,
resigned from their positions.^[478] <#cite_note-479> ^[479]
<#cite_note-480>


      Reactions

SNS proclaimed victory after the voting stations were closed, with
Brnabić saying at a press conference that "according to 50 percent of
processed polling stations, i.e. on a sample of 50 percent, the 'Serbia
Must Not Stop' list currently has 47.1 percent of popular vote".^[480]
<#cite_note-481> SNS was congratulated by Dačić and Milorad Dodik
<https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Milorad_Dodik>, the president of
Republika Srpska, and Katalin Novák <https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/
Katalin_Nov%C3%A1k>, the president of Hungary.^[481] <#cite_note-:
51-482> ^[482] <#cite_note-483> ^[483] <#cite_note-484> Vučić alleged
that a "an important country intervened in the election process of
Serbia in the most brutal way".^[484] <#cite_note-485>

Nestorović of MI–GIN said that "even though no one gave us a chance, we
became one of the four or five strongest parties"; he rejected
cooperating with SNS or SPN after the elections.^[485]
<#cite_note-486> /Danas/ newspaper described Nestorović as "the biggest
surprise" of the 2023 elections.^[486] <#cite_note-487> At a SPS press
conference, Dačić also said "this result is, as far as we are concerned,
unsatisfactory, and I will discuss with my colleagues from SPS what is
best for the party in the coming period. My personal opinion is that it
is necessary to find a new SPS leader".^[481] <#cite_note-:51-482>
Pásztor said that VMSZ "achieved the election result that we wanted" and
expressed joining the next SNS-led government.^[487] <#cite_note-488>

Miloš Bešić, a professor at the Faculty of Political Sciences, said that
the society in Serbia "is even more divided after the elections" and
argued that "the failure of right-wing parties is one of the main
impressions of the voting results".^[488] <#cite_note-:56-489> Bešić
also said that the attacks of SNS on SPS during the election campaign
was also shown in the elections, due to the decrease in support of SPS
and an increase in support of SNS.^[488] <#cite_note-:56-489> He,
however, noted that both SNS and SPS combined won fewer votes than in
the 2022 election.^[488] <#cite_note-:56-489>


      Government formation

On several occasions, Dačić has expressed his support for continuing to
work with SNS after the 2023 election.^[489] <#cite_note-:07-490> ^[490]
<#cite_note-:111-491> In October, Dačić had said: "I am convinced that
we will continue cooperation even after the victory in the December
elections, in the interest of Serbia, and a better future for all the
citizens of our country, as well as the Serbian people as a
whole."^[489] <#cite_note-:07-490> In an November interview with /
Insajder/, Dačić said that the goal of SPS is "to win a parliamentary
majority, together with SNS, because we alone cannot have a majority"
and that "the best solution for Serbia is ... that Vučić should be
president ... and Dacić should be prime minister."^[490] <#cite_note-:
111-491> Dačić later said, in regards to SNS forming a government with
SPS, that "[SPS] wants [to be in the government], but if they do not
want us, then there is no problem"; he has also criticised opposition
parties and described them as "a big fraud called DOS <https://
en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Democratic_Opposition_of_Serbia>".^[491]
<#cite_note-492> Other SPS politicians, like Paunović and Toma Fila
<https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Toma_Fila>, also expressed their support
for continuing to work with SNS after the elections.^[492]
<#cite_note-493> ^[493] <#cite_note-494> VMSZ also expressed its support
for extending the cooperation with SNS after the 2023 election.^[494]
<#cite_note-495>

Despite taking part with SNS in the Belgrade City assembly election,
Vučić said that the next government would not include SRS due to
programme differences, naming European Union as an example.^[495]
<#cite_note-496> Vučić has also expressed doubts in SPS during the
campaign period, while Brnabić has also criticised SPS officials such as
Ružić, her former cabinet minister.^[496] <#cite_note-497> ^[497]
<#cite_note-498> Vučević also said that "there are no guarantees that
SPS will ... switch to the other side."^[498] <#cite_note-499> Dušan
Spasojević, a Faculty of Political Sciences professor, said that the
"attacks on SPS are aimed to win back part of the voters who voted for
the Socialists in the last elections, and perhaps to take over part of
their voting base".^[499] <#cite_note-500> Popović of the Centre for
Practical Politics argued the same.^[500] <#cite_note-501>
